            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Hernandez is a tremendously versatile defender, as he played six different positions last year, despite appearing in just 40 major-league games. The 23-year-old is on the Dodgers' 40-man roster, and players as versatile as Hernandez usually work their way into a good chunk of major-league playing time. As he showed last year, he has some offensive upside when he does get on the field. Hernandez has good plate discipline and a sneaky amount of pop in his bat, though his ability to post a decent batting average is a dicey proposition at best. (<a href="https://twitter.com/scottstrandberg">Scott Strandberg</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>He won't likely break camp with the Dodgers, but I wouldn't be surprised at all if he ends up providing value in NL-only leagues at some point this season.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Enrique “Kiké” Hernandez appeared at no less than six positions for the Dodgers last year —making him valuable to Los Angeles but more of an enigma for fantasy owners, since he doesn’t have a clear role as of this writing. He’ll carry outfield and second base eligibility in most formats entering 2016, and might be compatible at shortstop in some leagues, but with Corey Seager now a full-time player, and that logjam in the outfield, Hernandez’s best (if not only) shot at regular playing time will be at third base, where (if his arm can handle it) he can compete with surprise late career bloomer Justin Turner for playing time. Hernandez, 24, slashed an impressive .307/.346/.490 last year in 218 plate appearances, benefitting immensely from a .364 average on balls in play. He did pop seven home runs after reaching double digits in his last two minor league seasons, but hits the ball on the ground too often and could see a regression in his 14.6% home run rate on fly balls. He also doesn’t walk enough to get on base at an average clip and has no speed. On the sunny side, he mashed lefties in the limited at-bats he saw against them, and could form a platoon with a lefty in the outfield if the infield is too crowded. Hernandez may have a path to playing time, but he's not yet more than a deep mixed-league option. (<a href="https://twitter.com/Karl_de_Vries">Karl de Vries</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Enrique Hernandez impressed in limited playing time last year, notching a .307 average and picking up middle infield and outfield eligibility. But he benefitted from some terrific batted ball luck and doesn’t help fantasy owners in any particular category, and without a full-time job entering 2016, he should be left for deeper mixed leagues.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>A year removed from leading the majors in wRC+ (235, not a typo) against left-handed pitchers in 2015, it looked like Hernandez was bound to repeat that success. He touched up Madison Bumgarner for a couple home runs on April 15 and was hitting .440/.481/.800 triple slash through the season's first couple weeks. But an unpredicted cold streak did him in. The rest of the way, Hernandez hit just .157/.258/.262 and was virtually unplayable for Dave Roberts, let alone a fantasy baseball league. Hernandez isn't nearly as good as he was in the first two weeks of the season, just as he isn't as bad as he was for the majority of the '16 season. He could be a nice bounce-back candidate in 2017, as his plate discipline numbers, on the whole, weren't that out of line with his 2015 numbers. The only one that stands out is his F-Strike%, which rose by almost 5 percent. Hitting 0-1 is a lot tougher than hitting 1-0. Because of his defensive versatility, it'd be hard to see Hernandez not on a 25-man roster for the majority of a season. But if he's hitting as poorly as he did in 2016, a trip to the minors could be in order. (Dustin Nosler)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Hernandez was one of baseball's most dangerous hitters against left-handed pitching in 2015 before falling flat on his face in 2016. Despite his versatility, he'll need to hit if he's to be valuable to an MLB team, and to have any fantasy value.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
